Ives</a>, and less frequently at <a href="/wiki/Bodmin" title="Bodmin">Bodmin</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;d&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Surfing_and_watersports">Surfing and watersports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cornwall&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Surfing and watersports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Pilot_Gigs_St_Mary%27s.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Pilot_Gigs_St_Mary%27s.jpg/220px-Pilot_Gigs_St_Mary%27s.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Pilot_Gigs_St_Mary%27s.jpg/330px-Pilot_Gigs_St_Mary%27s.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Pilot_Gigs_St_Mary%27s.jpg/440px-Pilot_Gigs_St_Mary%27s.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Pilot_Gigs_St_Mary%27s.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The world <a href="/wiki/Cornish_pilot_gig" title="Cornish pilot gig">pilot gig</a> rowing championships take place annually in the <a href="/wiki/Isles_of_Scilly" title="Isles of Scilly">Isles of Scilly</a>.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:GwithianSurfing.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/GwithianSurfing.jpg/220px-GwithianSurfing.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/GwithianSurfing.jpg/330px-GwithianSurfing.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/GwithianSurfing.jpg/440px-GwithianSurfing.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="683" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:GwithianSurfing.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Cornwall\'s north coast is known as a centre for <a href="/wiki/Surfing" title="Surfing">surfing</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Due to its long coastline, various maritime sports are popular in Cornwall, notably sailing and <a href="/wiki/Surfing" title="Surfing">surfing</a>. International events in both are held in Cornwall. Cornwall hosted the Inter-Celtic <a href="/wiki/Watersports" class="mw-redirect" title="Watersports">Watersports</a> Festival in 2006. Surfing in particular is very popular, as locations such as <a href="/wiki/Bude" title="Bude">Bude</a> and <a href="/wiki/Newquay" title="Newquay">Newquay</a> offer some of the best surf in the UK. <a href="/wiki/Cornish_pilot_gig" title="Cornish pilot gig">Pilot gig</a> rowing has been popular for many years and the World championships takes place annually on the <a href="/wiki/Isles_of_Scilly" title="Isles of Scilly">Isles of Scilly</a>. On 2 September 2007, 300 surfers at <a href="/wiki/Polzeath" title="Polzeath">Polzeath</a> beach set a new world record for the highest number of surfers riding the same wave as part of the Global Surf Challenge and part of a project called Earthwave to raise awareness about <a href="/wiki/Global_warming" title="Global warming">global warming</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Fencing">Fencing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cornwall&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Fencing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>As its population is comparatively small, and largely rural, Cornwall\'s contribution to British national <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Sport in the United Kingdom">sport in the United Kingdom</a> has been limited;<sup id="cite_ref-Clegg10_74-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Clegg10-74">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> the county\'s greatest successes have come in fencing. In 2014, half of the men\'s GB team fenced for Truro Fencing Club, and 3 Truro fencers appeared at the 2012 Olympics.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cornwall&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cornish_cuisine" title="Cornish cuisine">Cornish cuisine</a></div>\n<p>Cornwall has a strong culinary heritage. Surrounded on three sides by the sea amid fertile fishing grounds, Cornwall naturally has fresh seafood readily available; <a href="/wiki/Newlyn" title="Newlyn">Newlyn</a> is the largest fishing port in the UK by value of fish landed, and is known for its wide range of restaurants.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> Television chef <a href="/wiki/Rick_Stein" title="Rick Stein">Rick Stein</a> has long operated a fish restaurant in <a href="/wiki/Padstow" title="Padstow">Padstow</a> for this reason, and <a href="/wiki/Jamie_Oliver" title="Jamie Oliver">Jamie Oliver</a> chose to open his second restaurant, <a href="/wiki/Fifteen_(restaurant)" class="mw-redirect" title="Fifteen (restaurant)">Fifteen</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Watergate_Bay" title="Watergate Bay">Watergate Bay</a> near <a href="/wiki/Newquay" title="Newquay">Newquay</a>. <a href="/wiki/MasterChef_(UK_TV_series)" title="MasterChef (UK TV series)">MasterChef</a> host and founder of Smiths of Smithfield, <a href="/wiki/John_Torode" title="John Torode">John Torode</a>, in 2007 purchased Seiners in <a href="/wiki/Perranporth" title="Perranporth">Perranporth</a>. One famous local fish dish is <a href="/wiki/Stargazy_pie" title="Stargazy pie">Stargazy pie</a>, a fish-based pie in which the heads of the fish stick through the piecrust, as though "star-gazing". The pie is cooked as part of traditional celebrations for <a href="/wiki/Tom_Bawcock%27s_Eve" title="Tom Bawcock&#39;s Eve">Tom Bawcock\'s Eve</a>, but is not generally eaten at any other time.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cornish_pasty_-_cut.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Cornish_pasty_-_cut.jpeg/220px-Cornish_pasty_-_cut.jpeg" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Cornish_pasty_-_cut.jpeg/330px-Cornish_pasty_-_cut.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Cornish_pasty_-_cut.jpeg/440px-Cornish_pasty_-_cut.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="1448" data-file-height="973" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cornish_pasty_-_cut.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Pasty" title="Pasty">Cornish pasty</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Cornwall is perhaps best known though for its <a href="/wiki/Pasty" title="Pasty">pasties</a>, a savoury dish made with pastry. Today\'s pasties usually contain a filling of beef steak, onion, potato and <a href="/wiki/Swedish_turnip" class="mw-redirect" title="Swedish turnip">swede</a> with salt and white pepper, but historically pasties had a variety of different fillings. "Turmut, \'tates and mate" (i.e. "Turnip, potatoes and meat", turnip being the Cornish and Scottish term for swede, itself an abbreviation of \'Swedish Turnip\', the British term for <a href="/wiki/Rutabaga" title="Rutabaga">rutabaga</a>) describes a filling once very common. For instance, the licky pasty contained mostly leeks, and the herb pasty contained watercress, parsley, and shallots.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> Pasties are often locally referred to as <i>oggies</i>. Historically, pasties were also often made with sweet fillings such as jam, apple and blackberry, plums or cherries.<sup id="cite_ref-Martin_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Martin-82">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>\nThe wet climate and relatively poor soil of Cornwall make it unsuitable for growing many arable crops. However, it is ideal for growing the rich grass required for dairying, leading to the production of Cornwall\'s other famous export, <a href="/wiki/Clotted_cream" title="Clotted cream">clotted cream</a>. This forms the basis for many local specialities including Cornish <a href="/wiki/Fudge" title="Fudge">fudge</a> and Cornish <a href="/wiki/Ice_cream" title="Ice cream">ice cream</a>. Cornish clotted cream has <a href="/wiki/Protected_Geographical_Status" class="mw-redirect" title="Protected Geographical Status">Protected Geographical Status</a> under EU law,<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> and cannot be made anywhere else. Its principal manufacturer is <a href="/wiki/A._E._Rodda_%26_Son" class="mw-redirect" title="A. E. Rodda &amp; Son">A. E. Rodda &amp; Son</a> of Scorrier.\n</p><p>Local cakes and desserts include <a href="/wiki/Saffron_bun" title="Saffron bun">Saffron cake</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heavy_cake" title="Heavy cake">Cornish heavy (<i>hevva</i>) cake</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cornish_fairings" class="mw-redirect" title="Cornish fairings">Cornish fairings</a> biscuits, figgy \'obbin, <a href="/wiki/Cream_tea" title="Cream tea">Cream tea</a> and whortleberry pie.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>There are also many types of beers brewed in Cornwall&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 those produced by <a href="/wiki/Sharp%27s_Brewery" title="Sharp&#39;s Brewery">Sharp\'s Brewery</a>, <a href="/wiki/Skinner%27s_Brewery" title="Skinner&#39;s Brewery">Skinner\'s Brewery</a>, Keltek Brewery and <a href="/wiki/St_Austell_Brewery" title="St Austell Brewery">St Austell Brewery</a> are the best-known \xe2\x80\x93 including <a href="/wiki/Stout" title="Stout">stouts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ale" title="Ale">ales</a> and other beer types. There is some small scale production of wine, <a href="/wiki/Mead" title="Mead">mead</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cider" title="Cider">cider</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cornwall&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Cornwall" title="History of Cornwall">History of Cornwall</a> and <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Cornish_history" title="Timeline of Cornish history">Timeline of Cornish history</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Men-an-Tol.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Men-an-Tol.jpg/220px-Men-an-Tol.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Men-an-Tol.jpg/330px-Men-an-Tol.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Men-an-Tol.jpg/440px-Men-an-Tol.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Men-an-Tol.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/M%C3%AAn-an-Tol" title="M\xc3\xaan-an-Tol">M\xc3\xaan-an-Tol</a>.</div></div></div>\n<h3><span id="Prehistory.2C_Roman_and_post-Roman_periods"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Prehistory,_Roman_and_post-Roman_periods">Prehistory, Roman and post-Roman periods</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cornwall&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Prehistory, Roman and post-Roman periods">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Dumnonia" title="Dumnonia">Dumnonia</a></div>\n<p>The present human history of Cornwall begins with the reoccupation of Britain after the last Ice Age. The area now known as Cornwall was first inhabited in the <a href="/wiki/Palaeolithic" class="mw-redirect" title="Palaeolithic">Palaeolithic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mesolithic" title="Mesolithic">Mesolithic</a> periods. It continued to be occupied by <a href="/wiki/Prehistoric_Britain" title="Prehistoric Britain">Neolithic</a> and then <a href="/wiki/Bronze_Age_Britain" title="Bronze Age Britain">Bronze Age</a> people.\n</p><p>According to <a href="/wiki/John_T._Koch" title="John T. Koch">John T. Koch</a> and others, Cornwall in the Late Bronze Age was part of a maritime trading-networked culture called the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Bronze_Age" title="Atlantic Bronze Age">Atlantic Bronze Age</a>, in modern-day Ireland, England, France, Spain and Portugal.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During the <a href="/wiki/British_Iron_Age" title="British Iron Age">British Iron Age</a>, Cornwall, like all of Britain south of the <a href="/wiki/Firth_of_Forth" title="Firth of Forth">Firth of Forth</a>, was inhabited by a <a href="/wiki/Celts" title="Celts">Celtic</a> people known as the <a href="/wiki/Britons_(Celtic_people)" class="mw-redirect" title="Britons (Celtic people)">Britons</a> with distinctive cultural relations to neighbouring <a href="/wiki/Wales" title="Wales">Wales</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brittany" title="Brittany">Brittany</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Common_Brittonic" title="Common Brittonic">Common Brittonic</a> spoken at the time eventually developed into several distinct tongues, including <a href="/wiki/Cornish_language" title="Cornish language">Cornish</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The first account of Cornwall comes from the 1st-century BC Sicilian Greek historian <a href="/wiki/Diodorus_Siculus" title="Diodorus Siculus">Diodorus Siculus</a>, supposedly quoting or paraphrasing the 4th-century BCE geographer <a href="/wiki/Pytheas" title="Pytheas">Pytheas</a>, who had sailed to Britain:\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303468">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>The inhabitants of that part of Britain called <i>Belerion</i> (or Land\'s End) from their intercourse with foreign merchants, are civilised in their manner of life. They prepare the tin, working very carefully the earth in which it is produced ... Here then the merchants buy the tin from the natives and carry it over to <a href="/wiki/Gaul" title="Gaul">Gaul</a>, and after travelling overland for about thirty days, they finally bring their loads on horses to the mouth of the Rh\xc3\xb4ne.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>\n</p></blockquote>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:England_Celtic_tribes_-_South.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/England_Celtic_tribes_-_South.svg/220px-England_Celtic_tribes_-_South.svg.png" width="220" height="119" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/England_Celtic_tribes_-_South.svg/330px-England_Celtic_tribes_-_South.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/England_Celtic_tribes_-_South.svg/440px-England_Celtic_tribes_-_South.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1375" data-file-height="743" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:England_Celtic_tribes_-_South.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Celtic tribes of Southern Britain.</div></div></div>\n<p>The identity of these merchants is unknown. It has been theorised that they were <a href="/wiki/Phoenicia" title="Phoenicia">Phoenicians</a>, but there is no evidence for this.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> Professor Timothy Champion, discussing Diodorus Siculus\'s comments on the tin trade, states that "Diodorus never actually says that the Phoenicians sailed to Cornwall. In fact, he says quite the opposite: the production of Cornish tin was in the hands of the natives of Cornwall, and its transport to the Mediterranean was organised by local merchants, by sea and then over land through France, well outside Phoenician control."<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> (For further discussion of tin mining see the section on the economy below.)\n</p><p>There is little evidence that <a href="/wiki/Roman_Britain" title="Roman Britain">Roman rule</a> was effective west of <a href="/wiki/Exeter" title="Exeter">Exeter</a> in Devon and few Roman remains have been found. However, after 410, Cornwall appears to have reverted to rule by Romano-Celtic chieftains of the <a href="/wiki/Cornovii_(Cornwall)" title="Cornovii (Cornwall)">Cornovii</a> tribe as part of <a href="/wiki/Dumnonia" title="Dumnonia">Dumnonia</a>, including one <a href="/wiki/Marcus_Cunomorus" class="mw-redirect" title="Marcus Cunomorus">Marcus Cunomorus</a>, with at least one significant power base at <a href="/wiki/Tintagel" title="Tintagel">Tintagel</a>.\n</p><p>"King" <a href="/wiki/Mark_of_Cornwall" title="Mark of Cornwall">Mark of Cornwall</a> is a semi-historical figure known from Welsh literature, the <a href="/wiki/Matter_of_Britain" title="Matter of Britain">Matter of Britain</a>, and in particular, the later Norman-Breton medieval romance of <a href="/wiki/Tristan_and_Yseult" class="mw-redirect" title="Tristan and Yseult">Tristan and Yseult</a>, where he is regarded as a close relative of <a href="/wiki/King_Arthur" title="King Arthur">King Arthur</a>, himself usually considered to be born of the Cornish people in folklore traditions derived from <a href="/wiki/Geoffrey_of_Monmouth" title="Geoffrey of Monmouth">Geoffrey of Monmouth</a>\'s <i><a href="/wiki/Historia_Regum_Britanniae" title="Historia Regum Britanniae">Historia Regum Britanniae</a></i>.\n</p><p>Archaeology supports ecclesiastical, literary and legendary evidence for some relative economic stability and close cultural ties between the sub-Roman <a href="/wiki/Westcountry" class="mw-redirect" title="Westcountry">Westcountry</a>, South Wales, Brittany and Ireland through the fifth and sixth centuries.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Conflict_with_Wessex">Conflict with Wessex</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cornwall&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Conflict with Wessex">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Deorham" title="Battle of Deorham">Battle of Deorham</a> in 577 saw the separation of <a href="/wiki/Dumnonia" title="Dumnonia">Dumnonia</a> (and therefore Cornwall) from Wales, following which the <a href="/wiki/Dumnonii" title="Dumnonii">Dumnonii</a> often came into conflict with the expanding English kingdom of <a href="/wiki/Wessex" title="Wessex">Wessex</a>. The <i><a href="/wiki/Annales_Cambriae" title="Annales Cambriae">Annales Cambriae</a></i> report that in 722 AD the Britons of Cornwall won a battle at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Hehil" title="Battle of Hehil">"Hehil"</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> It seems likely that the enemy the Cornish fought was a West Saxon force, as evidenced by the naming of <a href="/wiki/King_Ine" class="mw-redirect" title="King Ine">King Ine</a> of Wessex and his kinsman Nonna in reference to an earlier Battle of Lining in 710.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <i>Anglo-Saxon Chronicle</i> stated in 815 (adjusted date) "and in this year king Ecgbryht raided in Cornwall from east to west." and thenceforth apparently held it as a ducatus or dukedom annexed to his regnum or kingdom of Wessex, but not wholly incorporated with it.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> The <i>Anglo-Saxon Chronicle</i> states that in 825 (adjusted date) a battle took place between the Wealas (Cornish) and the Defnas (men of Devon) at <a href="/wiki/Gafulforda" class="mw-redirect" title="Gafulforda">Gafulforda</a>. In the same year Ecgbert, as a later document expresses it, "disposed of their territory as it seemed fit to him, giving a tenth part of it to God." In other words, he incorporated Cornwall <a href="/wiki/Church_polity" class="mw-redirect" title="Church polity">ecclesiastically</a> with the West Saxon <a href="/wiki/Diocese_of_Sherborne" class="mw-redirect" title="Diocese of Sherborne">diocese of Sherborne</a>, and endowed <a href="/wiki/Eahlstan" title="Eahlstan">Eahlstan</a>, his fighting bishop, who took part in the campaign, with an extensive Cornish estate consisting of <a href="/wiki/Callington,_Cornwall" title="Callington, Cornwall">Callington</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lawhitton" title="Lawhitton">Lawhitton</a>, both in the <a href="/wiki/River_Tamar" title="River Tamar">Tamar</a> valley, and <a href="/wiki/Pawton" class="mw-redirect" title="Pawton">Pawton</a> near <a href="/wiki/Padstow" title="Padstow">Padstow</a>.\n</p><p>In 838, the Cornish and their Danish allies were defeated by Egbert in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Hingston_Down" title="Battle of Hingston Down">Battle of Hingston Down</a> at Hengestesdune (probably <a href="/wiki/Hingston_Down" title="Hingston Down">Hingston Down</a> in Cornwall). In 875, the last recorded king of Cornwall, <a href="/wiki/Donyarth" title="Donyarth">Dumgarth</a>, is said to have drowned.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> Around the 880s, Anglo-Saxons from Wessex had established modest land holdings in the eastern part of Cornwall; notably <a href="/wiki/Alfred_the_Great" title="Alfred the Great">Alfred the Great</a> who had acquired a few estates.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/William_of_Malmesbury" title="William of Malmesbury">William of Malmesbury</a>, writing around 1120, says that King <a href="/wiki/Athelstan" class="mw-redirect" title="Athelstan">Athelstan</a> of England (924\xe2\x80\x93939) fixed the boundary between English and Cornish people at the east bank of the River Tamar.<sup id="cite_ref-Stenton,_F._M._1947_p._337_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stenton,_F._M._1947_p._337-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Breton.E2.80.93Norman_period"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Breton\xe2\x80\x93Norman_period">Breton\xe2\x80\x93Norman period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cornwall&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Breton\xe2\x80\x93Norman period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kernow_Hundreds.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Kernow_Hundreds.png/220px-Kernow_Hundreds.png" width="220" height="143" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Kernow_Hundreds.png/330px-Kernow_Hundreds.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Kernow_Hundreds.png/440px-Kernow_Hundreds.png 2x" data-file-width="821" data-file-height="532" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kernow_Hundreds.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The ancient <a href="/wiki/Hundreds_of_Cornwall" title="Hundreds of Cornwall">Hundreds of Cornwall</a></div></div></div>\n<p>One interpretation of the <a href="/wiki/Domesday_Book" title="Domesday Book">Domesday Book</a> is that by this time the native Cornish landowning class had been almost completely dispossessed and replaced by English landowners, particularly <a href="/wiki/Harold_Godwinson" title="Harold Godwinson">Harold Godwinson</a> himself. However, the <a href="/wiki/Bodmin_manumissions" title="Bodmin manumissions">Bodmin manumissions</a> show that two leading Cornish figures nominally had Saxon names, but these were both glossed with native Cornish names.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> Naming evidence cited by medievalist <a href="/wiki/Edith_Ditmas" title="Edith Ditmas">Edith Ditmas</a> suggests that many post-Conquest landowners in Cornwall were Breton allies of the Normans<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> and further proposed this period for the early composition of the <a href="/wiki/Tristan_and_Iseult" title="Tristan and Iseult">Tristan and Iseult</a> cycle by poets such as <a href="/wiki/Beroul" class="mw-redirect" title="Beroul">Beroul</a> from a pre-existing shared Brittonic oral tradition.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Soon after the <a href="/wiki/Norman_conquest_of_England" title="Norman conquest of England">Norman conquest</a> most of the land was transferred to the new Breton\xe2\x80\x93Norman aristocracy, with the lion\'s share going to <a href="/wiki/Robert,_Count_of_Mortain" title="Robert, Count of Mortain">Robert, Count of Mortain</a>, half-brother of <a href="/wiki/William_I_of_England" class="mw-redirect" title="William I of England">King William</a> and the largest landholder in England after the king with his stronghold at <a href="/wiki/Trematon_Castle" title="Trematon Castle">Trematon Castle</a> near the mouth of the Tamar.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> Cornwall and Devon west of <a href="/wiki/Dartmoor" title="Dartmoor">Dartmoor</a> showed a very different type of settlement pattern from that of Saxon Wessex and places continued, even after 1066, to be named in the <a href="/wiki/Celts" title="Celts">Celtic</a> Cornish tradition with <a href="/wiki/Saxon_architecture" class="mw-redirect" title="Saxon architecture">Saxon architecture</a> being uncommon.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Later_medieval_administration_and_society">Later medieval administration and society</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cornwall&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Later medieval administration and society">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Subsequently, however, Norman absentee landlords became replaced by a new Cornu-Norman elite including scholars such as <a href="/wiki/Richard_Rufus_of_Cornwall" title="Richard Rufus of Cornwall">Richard Rufus of Cornwall</a>. These families eventually became the new ruling class of Cornwall (typically speaking Norman French, Breton-Cornish, Latin and eventually English), many becoming involved in the operation of the <a href="/wiki/Stannary_Parliament" class="mw-redirect" title="Stannary Parliament">Stannary Parliament</a> system, Earldom and eventually the Duchy.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Cornish_language" title="Cornish language">Cornish language</a> continued to be spoken and it acquired a number of characteristics establishing its identity as a separate language from <a href="/wiki/Breton_language" title="Breton language">Breton</a>.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Stannary_parliaments">Stannary parliaments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cornwall&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Stannary parliaments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Stannary_Courts_and_Parliaments" class="mw-redirect" title="Stannary Courts and Parliaments">Stannary Courts and Parliaments</a></div>\n<p>The stannary parliaments and stannary courts were legislative and legal institutions in Cornwall and in Devon (in the Dartmoor area). The stannary courts administered <a href="/wiki/Equity_(law)" title="Equity (law)">equity</a> for the region\'s tin-miners and tin mining interests, and they were also courts of record for the towns dependent on the mines. The separate and powerful government institutions available to the tin miners reflected the enormous importance of the tin industry to the English economy during the Middle Ages. Special laws for tin miners pre-date written legal codes in Britain, and ancient traditions exempted everyone connected with tin mining in Cornwall and Devon from any jurisdiction other than the stannary courts in all but the most exceptional circumstances.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Piracy_and_smuggling">Piracy and smuggling</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cornwall&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Piracy and smuggling">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Cornish piracy was active during the Elizabethan era on the west coast of Britain.<sup id="cite_ref-Matthew_1924_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Matthew_1924-104">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> Cornwall is well known for its <a href="/wiki/Wrecking_(shipwreck)" title="Wrecking (shipwreck)">wreckers</a> who preyed on ships passing Cornwall\'s rocky coastline. During the 17th and 18th centuries Cornwall was a major <a href="/wiki/Smuggling" title="Smuggling">smuggling</a> area.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics_and_administration">Politics and administration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cornwall&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Politics and administration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Cornwall" title="Politics of Cornwall">Politics of Cornwall</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cornish_national_identity">Cornish national identity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cornwall&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Cornish national identity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Cornish_nationalism" title="Cornish nationalism">Cornish nationalism</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cornish_National_Identity_2011_Census.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Cornish_National_Identity_2011_Census.png/220px-Cornish_National_Identity_2011_Census.png" width="220" height="205" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Cornish_National_Identity_2011_Census.png/330px-Cornish_National_Identity_2011_Census.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Cornish_National_Identity_2011_Census.png/440px-Cornish_National_Identity_2011_Census.png 2x" data-file-width="18793" data-file-height="17495" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cornish_National_Identity_2011_Census.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The percentage of respondents who gave "Cornish" as an answer to the National Identity question in the 2011 census.</div></div></div><p> Cornwall is recognised by Cornish and Celtic political groups as one of six Celtic nations, alongside <a href="/wiki/Brittany" title="Brittany">Brittany</a>, Ireland, the <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Man" title="Isle of Man">Isle of Man</a>, Scotland and Wales.<sup id="cite_ref-Teverson_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Teverson-105">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Mebyon_Kernow_1_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mebyon_Kernow_1-106">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-League_1_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-League_1-107">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Celtic_Congress_1_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Celtic_Congress_1-108">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> (The <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Man_Government" title="Isle of Man Government">Isle of Man Government</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Welsh_Government" title="Welsh Government">Welsh Government</a> also recognise <a href="/wiki/Asturias" title="Asturias">Asturias</a> and <a href="/wiki/Galicia_(Spain)" title="Galicia (Spain)">Galicia</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-Welsh_Government_1_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Welsh_Government_1-109">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Vannin_1_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vannin_1-110">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> Cornwall is represented, as one of the Celtic nations, at the <i><a href="/wiki/Festival_Interceltique_de_Lorient" title="Festival Interceltique de Lorient">Festival Interceltique de Lorient</a></i>, an annual celebration of Celtic culture held in Brittany.<sup id="cite_ref-Festival_1_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Festival_1-111">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Cornwall Council consider Cornwall\'s unique cultural heritage and distinctiveness to be one of the area\'s major assets. They see Cornwall\'s language, landscape, Celtic identity, political history, patterns of settlement, maritime tradition, industrial heritage, and non-conformist tradition, to be among the features making up its "distinctive" culture.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> However, it is uncertain how many of the people living in Cornwall consider themselves to be Cornish; results from different surveys (including the national census) have varied. In the 2001 census, 7 per cent of people in Cornwall identified themselves as Cornish, rather than British or English. However, activists have argued that this underestimated the true number as there was no explicit "Cornish" option included in the official census form.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> Subsequent surveys have suggested that as many as 44 per cent identify as Cornish.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> Many people in Cornwall say that this issue would be resolved if a Cornish option became available on the census.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> The question and content recommendations for the 2011 Census provided an explanation of the process of selecting an ethnic identity which is relevant to the understanding of the often quoted figure of 37,000 who claim Cornish identity.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 24 April 2014 it was announced that Cornish people have been granted minority status under the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European</a> <a href="/wiki/Framework_Convention_for_the_Protection_of_National_Minorities" title="Framework Convention for the Protection of National Minorities">Framework Convention for the Protection of National Minorities</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc_minority_status_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc_minority_status-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Local_politics">Local politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cornwall&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Local politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:New_County_Hall.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/New_County_Hall.jpg/220px-New_County_Hall.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/New_County_Hall.jpg/330px-New_County_Hall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/New_County_Hall.jpg/440px-New_County_Hall.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:New_County_Hall.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Cornwall_Council" title="Cornwall Council">Cornwall Council</a>\'s headquarters in <a href="/wiki/Truro" title="Truro">Truro</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:CornwallConstituencies2010.gif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/CornwallConstituencies2010.gif/220px-CornwallConstituencies2010.gif" width="220" height="205" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/CornwallConstituencies2010.gif/330px-CornwallConstituencies2010.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/CornwallConstituencies2010.gif/440px-CornwallConstituencies2010.gif 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="1116" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:CornwallConstituencies2010.gif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>From the 2010 general election, Cornwall has had six parliamentary constituencies</div></div></div>\n<p>With the exception of the <a href="/wiki/Isles_of_Scilly" title="Isles of Scilly">Isles of Scilly</a>, Cornwall is governed by a <a href="/wiki/Unitary_authority" title="Unitary authority">unitary authority</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cornwall_Council" title="Cornwall Council">Cornwall Council</a>, based in <a href="/wiki/Truro" title="Truro">Truro</a>. The Crown Court is based at the Courts of Justice in Truro. Magistrates\' Courts are found in Truro (but at a different location to the Crown Court) and at Bodmin.\n</p><p>The Isles of Scilly form part of the <a href="/wiki/Ceremonial_county" class="mw-redirect" title="Ceremonial county">ceremonial county</a> of Cornwall,<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> and have, at times, been served by the same county administration. Since 1890 they have been administered by their own <a href="/wiki/Unitary_authority" title="Unitary authority">unitary authority</a>, the Council of the Isles of Scilly. They are grouped with Cornwall for other administrative purposes, such as the <a href="/wiki/National_Health_Service_(England)" title="National Health Service (England)">National Health Service</a> and <a href="/wiki/Devon_and_Cornwall_Constabulary" class="mw-redirect" title="Devon and Cornwall Constabulary">Devon and Cornwall Police</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-iosuatt_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iosuatt-118">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-iosrdtt_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iosrdtt-119">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Before reorganisation on 1 April 2009, council functions throughout the rest of Cornwall were organised in two tiers, with a county council and district councils for its six districts, <a href="/wiki/Caradon" title="Caradon">Caradon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carrick,_Cornwall" title="Carrick, Cornwall">Carrick</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kerrier" title="Kerrier">Kerrier</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Cornwall" title="North Cornwall">North Cornwall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Penwith" title="Penwith">Penwith</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Restormel" title="Restormel">Restormel</a>. While projected to streamline services, cut red tape and save around \xc2\xa317&#160;million a year, the reorganisation was met with wide opposition, with a poll in 2008 showing 89% disapproval from Cornish residents.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Cornwall_Council_election,_2009" title="Cornwall Council election, 2009">first elections</a> for the unitary authority were held on 4 June 2009. The council has 123 seats; the largest party (in 2017) is the Conservatives, with 46 seats. The Liberal Democrats are the second largest party, with 37 seats, with the Independents the third-largest grouping with 30.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Before the creation of the unitary council, the former county council had 82 seats, the majority of which were held by the Liberal Democrats, elected at the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_local_elections,_2005" title="United Kingdom local elections, 2005">2005 county council elections</a>. The six former districts had a total of 249 council seats, and the groups with greatest numbers of councillors were Liberal Democrats, Conservatives, and Independents.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Parliament_and_national_politics">Parliament and national politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cornwall&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Parliament and national politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Following a review by the <a href="/wiki/Boundary_Commission_for_England" class="mw-redirect" title="Boundary Commission for England">Boundary Commission for England</a> taking effect at the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_2010" title="United Kingdom general election, 2010">2010 general election</a>, Cornwall is divided into <a href="/wiki/List_of_Parliamentary_constituencies_in_Cornwall" title="List of Parliamentary constituencies in Cornwall">six</a> <a href="/wiki/County_constituencies" class="mw-redirect" title="County constituencies">county constituencies</a> to elect MPs to the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Commons_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="House of Commons of the United Kingdom">House of Commons of the United Kingdom</a>.\n</p><p>Before the 2010 boundary changes Cornwall had five constituencies all of which were won by <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Democrats_(UK)" title="Liberal Democrats (UK)">Liberal Democrats</a> in the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_2005" title="United Kingdom general election, 2005">2005 general election</a>. At the 2010 general election Liberal Democrat candidates won three constituencies and Conservative candidates won three constituencies (<i>see also <a href="/wiki/2010_United_Kingdom_general_election_result_in_Cornwall" class="mw-redirect" title="2010 United Kingdom general election result in Cornwall">2010 United Kingdom general election result in Cornwall</a></i>). At the <a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Kingdom_general_election,_2015_(Cornwall)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="United Kingdom general election, 2015 (Cornwall) (page does not exist)">2015 general election</a> all six Cornish seats were won by Conservative candidates. All these conservative MPs retained their seats in the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_2017" title="United Kingdom general election, 2017">2017 general election</a>\n</p><p>Until 1832, Cornwall had 44 MPs \xe2\x80\x93 more than any other county \xe2\x80\x93 reflecting the importance of tin to the Crown.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> Most of the increase in numbers of MPs came between 1529 and 1584 after which there was no change until 1832.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Devolution_movement">Devolution movement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cornwall&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Devolution movement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Cornish nationalists have organised into two political parties: Mebyon Kernow, formed in 1951, and the <a href="/wiki/Cornish_Nationalist_Party" title="Cornish Nationalist Party">Cornish Nationalist Party</a>. In addition to the political parties, there are various interest groups such as the <a href="/wiki/Revived_Cornish_Stannary_Parliament" title="Revived Cornish Stannary Parliament">Revived Cornish Stannary Parliament</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Celtic_League_(political_organisation)" class="mw-redirect" title="Celtic League (political organisation)">Celtic League</a>. The Cornish Constitutional Convention was formed in 2000 as a cross-party organisation including representatives from the private, public and voluntary sectors to campaign for the creation of a <a href="/wiki/Cornish_Assembly" title="Cornish Assembly">Cornish Assembly</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ccc_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ccc-127">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> along the lines of the <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_for_Wales" title="National Assembly for Wales">National Assembly for Wales</a>, <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland_Assembly" title="Northern Ireland Assembly">Northern Ireland Assembly</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Parliament" title="Scottish Parliament">Scottish Parliament</a>. Between 5 March 2000 and December 2001, the campaign collected the signatures of 41,650 Cornish residents endorsing the call for a devolved assembly, along with 8,896 signatories from outside Cornwall. The resulting petition was presented to the Prime Minister, <a href="/wiki/Tony_Blair" title="Tony Blair">Tony Blair</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_8-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> The Liberal Democrats recognise Cornwall\'s claims for greater autonomy, as do the <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Party_(UK,_1989)" title="Liberal Party (UK, 1989)">Liberal Party</a>.\n</p>\n<dl><dd>"The new single council is also the opportunity to gain more control over local issues from regional and national Government bureaucrats \xe2\x80\x93 the first step on our way to a Cornish Assembly." \xe2\x80\x93 The Liberal Democrat Manifesto for 2009</dd></dl>\n<p>An additional political issue is the recognition of the <a href="/wiki/Cornish_people" title="Cornish people">Cornish people</a> as a minority.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cornwall&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Cornwall" title="Economy of Cornwall">Economy of Cornwall</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:FalmouthDocks.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/FalmouthDocks.jpg/220px-FalmouthDocks.jpg" width="220" height="159" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/FalmouthDocks.jpg/330px-FalmouthDocks.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/FalmouthDocks.jpg/440px-FalmouthDocks.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1500" data-file-height="1082" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:FalmouthDocks.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Falmouth Docks is the major port of Cornwall, and one of the largest <a href="/wiki/Natural_harbour" class="mw-redirect" title="Natural harbour">natural harbours</a> in the world</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Eden_project1.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Eden_project1.JPG/220px-Eden_project1.JPG" width="220" height="171" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Eden_project1.JPG/330px-Eden_project1.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Eden_project1.JPG/440px-Eden_project1.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1799" data-file-height="1396" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Eden_project1.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Eden_Project" title="Eden Project">Eden Project</a> near St Austell, Cornwall\'s largest tourist attraction in terms of visitor numbers</div></div></div>\n<p>Cornwall is one of the poorest parts of the United Kingdom in terms of per capita GDP and average household incomes. At the same time, parts of the county, especially on the coast, have high house prices, driven up by demand from relatively wealthy retired people and second-home owners.<sup id="cite_ref-Indypoverty_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Indypoverty-129">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Gross_value_added" title="Gross value added">GVA</a> per head was 65% of the UK average for 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> The GDP per head for Cornwall and the <a href="/wiki/Isles_of_Scilly" title="Isles of Scilly">Isles of Scilly</a> was 79.2% of the EU-27 average for 2004, the UK per head average was 123.0%.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> In 2011, the latest available figures, Cornwall\'s (including the Isles of Scilly) measure of wealth was 64% of the European average per capita.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Historically <a href="/wiki/Mining_in_Cornwall_and_Devon" title="Mining in Cornwall and Devon">mining of tin</a> (and later also of copper) was important in the Cornish economy. The first reference to this appears to be by Pytheas: <i>see above</i>. <a href="/wiki/Julius_Caesar" title="Julius Caesar">Julius Caesar</a> was the last classical writer to mention the <a href="/wiki/Tin" title="Tin">tin</a> trade, which appears to have declined during the Roman occupation.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> The tin trade revived in the Middle Ages and its importance to the Kings of England resulted in certain privileges being granted to the tinners; the <a href="/wiki/Cornish_Rebellion_of_1497" class="mw-redirect" title="Cornish Rebellion of 1497">Cornish Rebellion of 1497</a> is attributed to grievances of the tin miners.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> In the mid-19th century, however, the tin trade again fell into decline. Other <a href="/wiki/Primary_industries" class="mw-redirect" title="Primary industries">primary industries</a> that have declined since the 1960s include <a href="/wiki/China_clay" class="mw-redirect" title="China clay">china clay</a> production, fishing and farming.\n</p><p>Today, the Cornish economy depends heavily on its tourist industry, which makes up around a quarter of the economy. The official measures of deprivation and poverty at district and \'sub-ward\' level show that there is great variation in poverty and prosperity in Cornwall with some areas among the poorest in England and others among the top half in prosperity. For example, the ranking of 32,482 sub-wards in England in the index of multiple deprivation (2006) ranged from 819th (part of Penzance East) to 30,899th (part of Saltash Burraton in Caradon), where the lower number represents the greater deprivation.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Cornwall is one of two UK areas designated as \'less developed regions\' which qualify for Cohesion\nPolicy grants from the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> It was granted <a href="/wiki/Objective_1" class="mw-redirect" title="Objective 1">Objective 1</a> status by the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a> for 2000 to 2006,<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> followed by further rounds of funding known as \'Convergence Funding\' from 2007 to 2013<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> and \'Growth Programme\' for 2014 to 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cornwall&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Par_Station_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1073711.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Par_Station_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1073711.jpg/220px-Par_Station_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1073711.jpg" width="220" height="330" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Par_Station_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1073711.jpg/330px-Par_Station_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1073711.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/91/Par_Station_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1073711.jpg 2x" data-file-width="427" data-file-height="640" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Par_Station_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1073711.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Par_railway_station" title="Par railway station">Par railway station</a> with a <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_43_(HST)" title="British Rail Class 43 (HST)">British Rail Class 43 (HST)</a> introduced by <a href="/wiki/British_Rail" title="British Rail">British Rail</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Cornish_Main_Line" title="Cornish Main Line">Cornish Main Line</a> by the <a href="/wiki/InterCity_(British_Rail)" title="InterCity (British Rail)">InterCity</a> sector.</div></div></div>\n<p>Tourism is estimated to contribute up to<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (June 2018)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> 24% of Cornwall\'s gross domestic product.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> In 2011 tourism brought \xc2\xa31.85 billion into the Cornish economy.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> Cornwall\'s unique culture, spectacular landscape and mild climate make it a popular tourist destination, despite being somewhat distant from the United Kingdom\'s main centres of population. Surrounded on three sides by the <a href="/wiki/English_Channel" title="English Channel">English Channel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Celtic_Sea" title="Celtic Sea">Celtic Sea</a>, Cornwall has many miles of beaches and cliffs; the <a href="/wiki/South_West_Coast_Path" title="South West Coast Path">South West Coast Path</a> follows a complete circuit of both coasts. Other tourist attractions include moorland, country gardens, museums, historic and prehistoric sites, and wooded valleys. Five million tourists visit Cornwall each year, mostly drawn from within the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> Visitors to Cornwall are served by the airport at <a href="/wiki/Newquay" title="Newquay">Newquay</a>, whilst private jets, charters and helicopters are also served by <a href="/wiki/Perranporth" title="Perranporth">Perranporth</a> airfield; nightsleeper and daily rail services run between Cornwall, London and other regions of the UK. Cornwall has a tourism-based <a href="/w/index.php?title=Seasonal_economy&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Seasonal economy (page does not exist)">seasonal economy</a>.\n</p><p>Newquay and <a href="/wiki/Porthtowan" title="Porthtowan">Porthtowan</a> are popular destinations for surfers. In recent years, the <a href="/wiki/Eden_Project" title="Eden Project">Eden Project</a> near <a href="/wiki/St_Austell" title="St Austell">St Austell</a> has been a major financial success, drawing one in eight of Cornwall\'s visitors in 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the summer of 2018, due to the recognition of its beaches and weather through social media and the marketing of travel companies, the county received about 20 per cent more visitors on the usual 4.5 million figure. The sudden rise and demand of tourism in the county caused multiple traffic and safety issues on the coastal areas.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Internet">Internet</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cornwall&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Internet">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Cornwall is the landing point for twenty-two of the world\'s fastest high-speed undersea and transatlantic fibre optic cables, making Cornwall an important hub within Europe\'s Internet infrastructure.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Superfast_broadband" class="mw-redirect" title="Superfast broadband">Superfast Cornwall</a> project completed in 2015,<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> and saw 95% of Cornish houses and businesses connected to a fibre-based broadband network, with over 90% of properties able to connect with speeds above 24Mbit/s.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fishing">Fishing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cornwall&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Fishing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tin-mining-cornwall-c1890.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Tin-mining-cornwall-c1890.jpg/220px-Tin-mining-cornwall-c1890.jpg" width="220" height="99" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Tin-mining-cornwall-c1890.jpg/330px-Tin-mining-cornwall-c1890.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Tin-mining-cornwall-c1890.jpg/440px-Tin-mining-cornwall-c1890.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1283" data-file-height="579" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tin-mining-cornwall-c1890.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Redruth Mine in 1890</div></div></div>\n<p>Other industries include <a href="/wiki/Fishing_in_Cornwall" title="Fishing in Cornwall">fishing</a>, although this has been significantly re-structured by EU fishing policies (as of 2010 the Southwest Handline Fishermen\'s Association has started to revive the fishing industry).<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Agriculture">Agriculture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cornwall&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Agriculture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Agriculture, once an important part of the Cornish economy, has declined significantly relative to other industries. However, there is still a strong dairy industry, with products such as Cornish <a href="/wiki/Clotted_cream" title="Clotted cream">clotted cream</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mining">Mining</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cornwall&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Mining">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mining_in_Cornwall" class="mw-redirect" title="Mining in Cornwall">Mining in Cornwall</a></div>\n<p>Mining of tin and copper was also an industry, but today the derelict mine workings survive only as a <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" class="mw-redirect" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> However, the <a href="/wiki/Camborne_School_of_Mines" title="Camborne School of Mines">Camborne School of Mines</a>, which was relocated to <a href="/wiki/Tremough" class="mw-redirect" title="Tremough">Penryn</a> in 2004, is still a world centre of excellence in the field of mining and applied geology<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> and the grant of World Heritage status has attracted funding for conservation and heritage tourism.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/China_clay" class="mw-redirect" title="China clay">China clay</a> extraction has also been an important industry in the St Austell area, but this sector has been in decline, and this, coupled with increased mechanisation, has led to a decrease in employment in this sector, although the industry still employs around 2,133 people in Cornwall, and generates over \xc2\xa380 million to the local economy.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Aerospace">Aerospace</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cornwall&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Aerospace">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The county\'s newest industry is aviation: <a href="/wiki/Newquay_Airport" title="Newquay Airport">Newquay Airport</a> is the only national and international airport west of Exeter,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> and is the home of a growing business park with Enterprise Zone status, known as Aerohub. There are also plans to establish Spaceport Cornwall at Newquay, in partnership with Goonhilly satellite tracking station near Helston in south Cornwall.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cornwall&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Demography_of_Cornwall" title="Demography of Cornwall">Demography of Cornwall</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_settlements_in_Cornwall_by_population" title="List of settlements in Cornwall by population">List of settlements in Cornwall by population</a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Cornish_diaspora" title="Cornish diaspora">Cornish diaspora</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cornwall_population.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Cornwall_population.png/220px-Cornwall_population.png" width="220" height="141" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Cornwall_population.png/330px-Cornwall_population.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Cornwall_population.png/440px-Cornwall_population.png 2x" data-file-width="876" data-file-height="560" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cornwall_population.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Graph showing Cornwall\'s population from 1800 to 2000</div></div></div>\n<p>Cornwall\'s population was 537,400 at the last<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (June 2018)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> census, with a population density of 144 people per square kilometre, ranking it 40th and 41st respectively<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (June 2018)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> among the 47 counties of England. Cornwall\'s population was 95.7% <a href="/wiki/White_British" title="White British">White British</a> and has a relatively high rate of population growth. At 11.2% in the 1980s and 5.3% in the 1990s, it had the fifth-highest population growth rate of the counties of England.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> The natural change has been a small population decline, and the population increase is due to inward migration into Cornwall.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> According to the 1991 census, the population was 469,800.\n</p><p>Cornwall has a relatively high retired population, with 22.9% of pensionable age, compared with 20.3% for the United Kingdom as a whole.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> This may be due partly to Cornwall\'s rural and coastal geography increasing its popularity as a retirement location, and partly to outward migration of younger residents to more economically diverse areas.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education_system">Education system</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cornwall&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Education system">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_schools_in_Cornwall" title="List of schools in Cornwall">List of schools in Cornwall</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Old_School,_Grampound_Road_-_geograph.org.uk_-_200282.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/The_Old_School%2C_Grampound_Road_-_geograph.org.uk_-_200282.jpg/220px-The_Old_School%2C_Grampound_Road_-_geograph.org.uk_-_200282.jpg" width="220" height="152" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/The_Old_School%2C_Grampound_Road_-_geograph.org.uk_-_200282.jpg/330px-The_Old_School%2C_Grampound_Road_-_geograph.org.uk_-_200282.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/The_Old_School%2C_Grampound_Road_-_geograph.org.uk_-_200282.jpg/440px-The_Old_School%2C_Grampound_Road_-_geograph.org.uk_-_200282.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="441" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Old_School,_Grampound_Road_-_geograph.org.uk_-_200282.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Old School, Grampound Road</div></div></div>\n<p>Cornwall has a comprehensive education system, with 31 state and eight independent secondary schools. There are three further education colleges: <a href="/wiki/Truro_and_Penwith_College" title="Truro and Penwith College">Truro and Penwith College</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cornwall_College" title="Cornwall College">Cornwall College</a> and <a href="/wiki/Callywith_College" title="Callywith College">Callywith College</a> which opened in September 2017. The Isles of Scilly only has one school, while the former Restormel district has the highest school population, and school year sizes are around 200, with none above 270. Before the introduction of comprehensive schools there were a number of grammar schools and secondary modern schools, e.g. the schools that later became <a href="/wiki/Sir_James_Smith%27s_School" title="Sir James Smith&#39;s School">Sir James Smith\'s School</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wadebridge_School" title="Wadebridge School">Wadebridge School</a>. There are also primary schools in many villages and towns: e.g. <a href="/wiki/St_Mabyn_Church_of_England_Primary_School" title="St Mabyn Church of England Primary School">St Mabyn Church of England Primary School</a>.\n</p><p>Higher education is provided by <a href="/wiki/Falmouth_University" title="Falmouth University">Falmouth University</a>, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Exeter" title="University of Exeter">University of Exeter</a> (including <a href="/wiki/Camborne_School_of_Mines" title="Camborne School of Mines">Camborne School of Mines</a>), the <a href="/wiki/Combined_Universities_in_Cornwall" title="Combined Universities in Cornwall">Combined Universities in Cornwall</a>, Truro College and Penwith College (which combined in 2008 to make <a href="/wiki/Truro_and_Penwith_College" title="Truro and Penwith College">Truro and Penwith College</a>) and Cornwall College.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cornwall&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span portal</a></span></li></ul></div>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Index_of_Cornwall-related_articles" title="Index of Cornwall-related articles">Index of Cornwall-related articles</a></li>\n<li><a title="Tamar Valley AONB">Tamar Valley AONB</a></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cornwall&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;">\n<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-21"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-21">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/Eilert_Ekwall" title="Eilert Ekwall">Eilert Ekwall</a> who studied the place-names of England in the 1930s and 40s gives the following forms: Cornubia in Vita Melori &amp;c.; Middle Welsh Cerniu; Welsh Cernyw; Cornish: Kernow; (on) Cornwalum ASC 891; Cornwealum ASC(E) 997; "The Brit name goes back to *Cornavia probably derived from the tribal name Cornovii. OE Cornwealas means \'the Welsh in Cornwall\' this folk-name later became the name of the district".<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-31"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-31">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"<a href="/wiki/Wales" title="Wales">Wales</a>" is derived from the <a href="/wiki/Proto-Germanic_language" title="Proto-Germanic language">Proto-Germanic</a> word <i><a href="/wiki/Walhaz" title="Walhaz">Walhaz</a></i>, meaning "Romanised foreigner"; through <a href="/wiki/Old_English" title="Old English">Old English</a> <i>welis\xc4\x8b</i>, <i>w\xc3\xa6lis\xc4\x8b</i>, <i>wilis\xc4\x8b</i>, meaning "<a href="/wiki/Romano-British_culture" title="Romano-British culture">Romano-British</a>"; to <a href="/wiki/Modern_English" title="Modern English">Modern English</a> <i>Welsh</i>. The same etymology applies to Cornwall and to <a href="/wiki/Wallonia" title="Wallonia">Wallonia</a> in Belgium.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-33"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-33">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Britain\'s only other example of an ophiolite, the Shetland ophiolite, is older, and linked to the Grampian <a href="/wiki/Orogeny" title="Orogeny">Orogeny</a>.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-77"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-77">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The Bodmin hurl is held whenever the ceremony of <a href="/wiki/Beating_the_bounds" title="Beating the bounds">beating the bounds</a> takes place: each occasion must be five years or more after the last one.</span>\n</li>\n</ol></div></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cornwall&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; list-style-type: decimal;">\n<ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-1">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.oxforddictionaries.com/definition/american_english/Cornwall">"Cornwall: definition of Cornwall in Oxford dictionary (American English)"</a>. A total of \xe2\x82\xac458.1 million has been allocated to the new Programme for 2007\xe2\x80\x9313, which will be complemented by \xe2\x82\xac196 million of Convergence ESF funding to support learning and skills related activities.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Convergence+Programme+for+Cornwall+and+the+Isles+of+Scilly+Operational+Programme+2007%E2%80%9313&amp;rft.pub=Department+for+Communities+and+Local+Government&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.gov.uk%2Fgovernment%2Fuploads%2Fsystem%2Fuploads%2Fattachment_data%2Ffile%2F315870Cornwall&#95;__Isles_of_Scilly_Convergence_Operational_Programme_2007-14.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ACornwall" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/><sup class="noprint Inline-Template"><span style="white-space: nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Link_rot" title="Wikipedia:Link rot"><span title="&#160;Dead link since September 2016">permanent dead link</span></a></i>&#93;</span></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-140"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-140">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20160325225534/http://www.cornwall.gov.uk/business/europe/">"Cornwall Council \xe2\x80\x93 Business \xe2\x80\x93 Europe"</a>. <a href="/wiki/Cornwall_Council" title="Cornwall Council">Cornwall Council</a>. 18 December 2015.
